# Changelog

All notable changes to this repository are recorded in this file as lead-paragraph summaries. Detailed maintainer-level entries (full Added / Changed / Removed / Fixed / Security / Verification sections per change) are kept in [`.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md`](.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md). This is how this project's maintainer tracks the full audit trail. The convention is project-specific; forks may delete `.working/` and adopt their own approach to detailed change tracking. The mechanics are documented in the [`change-tracking` governance rule](dev-security/claude-rules/governance/change-tracking.md).

The format follows [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/) loosely; individual document versions follow semantic versioning as defined in [`specification-ingestion.md`](specification-ingestion.md). The library as a whole carries a Calendar Versioning (CalVer) version of the form `YYYY.MM.patch`; see [`specification-master-project.md`](specification-master-project.md) section 4.5.

## 2026-06-28, Library Version 2026.06.408, PR #430

Internal assistant-guidance change (invisible to adopters): codified a Communication conventions section in [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](.claude/CLAUDE.md) (no decorative honesty-intensifiers; use `IMPORTANT:` as the emphasis marker), maintainer-directed during the #429 close-out. Batches the #429 `/validate-pr` (0 findings) and `/retro` rows plus the pending-decisions resolution. Library `2026.06.407` to `2026.06.408`; README `1.9.278` to `1.9.279`.

## 2026-06-28, Library Version 2026.06.407, PR #429

**Close the two remaining low-severity trust-recovery tail findings (FR-188, FR-198).** FR-188 (from the 2026-06-27 `/fitness` pass): action 4.4 of [`supply-chain/procedure-supplier-exit-and-data-return.md`](supply-chain/procedure-supplier-exit-and-data-return.md) (`1.0.3` to `1.0.4`) instructed "escalate to Data Protection Officer" while the responsible party in the same row was already the DPO (a circular self-escalation); retargeted to "Legal and the Contract Owner", mirroring the document's own precedent (action 3.6 escalates a supplier contractual failure to Legal) and routing the documented residual risk to the exit decision authority. FR-198 (from the 2026-06-27 `/full-qa` pass): the [`compliance/matrix-grc-compliance-alignment.md`](compliance/matrix-grc-compliance-alignment.md) (`1.11.1` to `1.11.2`) Pseudonymisation row mapped `DSP-07, DSP-17, DSP-10`, where `DSP-10` ("Sensitive Data Transfer") was a loose third fit; replaced with `DSP-16` ("Data Retention and Deletion"), which is non-redundant (`DSP-08` would duplicate `DSP-07`'s "by design and default" theme) and grounded in the standard's scope item 3 (anonymisation as a retention strategy) plus its Related Documents link to the records-retention-and-destruction standard. Both codes verified against [`tools/ccm_aicm_reference.py`](tools/ccm_aicm_reference.py). [`taxonomy.yml`](taxonomy.yml) and [`docs/maturity-scorecard.md`](docs/maturity-scorecard.md) regenerated. Batches the #428 `/validate-pr` (0 findings) and `/retro` rows. Closes TODO items FR-188 and FR-198 (rotated to [`.working/DONE.md`](.working/DONE.md)). Library `2026.06.406` to `2026.06.407`; README `1.9.277` to `1.9.278`.

## 2026-06-28, Library Version 2026.06.406, PR #428

**Domain-wide privacy `PRI-*` CCM citation correction (the #427 out-of-window finding, completed).** The #427 `/validate-pr` sibling-file cross-check found the invalid-`PRI-*` class (CCM v4.1 has no PRI domain; `is_ccm_v41('PRI-0x')` is False) extended beyond the two procedures #427 fixed, into three more privacy files (seven citations). In [`privacy/policy-privacy-and-data-governance.md`](privacy/policy-privacy-and-data-governance.md) (`1.4.5` to `1.4.6`) the framework-mapping table's five rows: PRI-01 to **`GRC-06`** (Governance Responsibility Model), PRI-02 to **`DSP-12`** (Limitation of Purpose in Personal Data Processing), PRI-03 to **`DSP-10`** (Sensitive Data Transfer), PRI-04 to **`DSP-11`**, PRI-05 to **`SEF-08`**. In [`privacy/charter-privacy-management-programme.md`](privacy/charter-privacy-management-programme.md) (`1.5.0` to `1.5.1`) the range "PRI-01 through PRI-07" to the framework-level "Data Security and Privacy Lifecycle Management (DSP) domain" reference (a literal positional PRI-to-DSP renumber was rejected as fabricated). In [`privacy/procedure-privacy-impact-and-cross-border-transfer.md`](privacy/procedure-privacy-impact-and-cross-border-transfer.md) (`1.5.0` to `1.5.1`) the PIA row PRI-05 to **`DSP-09`** (Data Protection Impact Assessment). Three mappings were unambiguous (DSP-11, SEF-08, DSP-09); four were genuine semantic-mapping choices surfaced to the maintainer with recommendations and, on a no-answer graceful-degradation timeout, applied with the recommended evidence-backed defaults (GRC-06 / DSP-12 / DSP-10 / the DSP-domain reference) and recorded in [`.working/pending-decisions.md`](.working/pending-decisions.md) for confirm/redirect. [`taxonomy.yml`](taxonomy.yml) and [`docs/maturity-scorecard.md`](docs/maturity-scorecard.md) regenerated. ## 2026-06-28, Library Version 2026.06.401, PR #423

**New governance rule: `surface-counterproductive-instructions` (the eleventh pack rule).** Adds [`dev-security/claude-rules/governance/surface-counterproductive-instructions.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/governance/surface-counterproductive-instructions.md): a clear instruction is not automatically a correct one, so when executing it as given would reduce efficiency, effectiveness, or productivity, lower quality, destroy work already done, contradict a stated goal, or rest on a stale-state belief, the assistant stops, considers, and surfaces the concern with named options before acting (stop, consider, confirm), with a charitable-interpretation corollary (do not silently take a harmful literal reading; never revert or discard committed work without confirming) and an anti-over-ask calibration (fire only on material downside; one informed round; accept an informed override). Maintainer-directed after a prior session read a "wind down" instruction literally and silently reverted committed in-flight work it did not intend to destroy. Wired across the three gate-41 governance-rule enumeration surfaces (the pack [`README.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/README.md) tree plus its "two areas" prose, pack [`CLAUDE.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/CLAUDE.md), and project [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](.claude/CLAUDE.md)), the byte-identical [`.claude/rules/governance/surface-counterproductive-instructions.md`](.claude/rules/governance/surface-counterproductive-instructions.md) mirror and its [`tools/lint-claude-rules-sync.py`](tools/lint-claude-rules-sync.py) MIRROR_MAP entry, and the ten-to-eleven count advance in the [`tools/lint-collection-enumeration-consistency.py`](tools/lint-collection-enumeration-consistency.py) docstring and the [`dev-security/claude-rules/skills/guardrail-review/SKILL.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/skills/guardrail-review/SKILL.md) growth narrative. Pack `1.50.0` to `1.51.0`. This PR also folds in the abandoned PR #422 handoff's still-valid working state (the #421 `/validate-pr` and `/retro` rows, which never reached main), fixes the [`docs/adopter-guide.md`](docs/adopter-guide.md):60 "Core reference set" casing residue (the #421 `/validate-pr` Low finding, re-surfaced as Sweep 69 A-1), and batches the **Sweep 69** loop-break `/validate` row (#418..#421 deltas, one Low finding fixed). Library `2026.06.400` to `2026.06.401`; README `1.9.271` to `1.9.272`.

## 2026-06-27, Library Version 2026.06.395, PR #416

**FR-175: India DPDPA in-force-date reconciliation.** Closes the last remaining trust-recovery High. The privacy jurisdiction index ([`privacy/annex-privacy-jurisdiction-index.md`](privacy/annex-privacy-jurisdiction-index.md):137, the "2026 Update summary" bullet) said the Digital Personal Data Protection Rules 2025 were "published February 2025 and entered into force April 2025" with the Data Protection Board "commenced operations", an early-2025 projection that contradicted both [`privacy/jurisdictions/annex-privacy-india.md`](privacy/jurisdictions/annex-privacy-india.md):28 and the canonical [`governance/register-canonical-citations.md`](governance/register-canonical-citations.md):147. Per the finding's own instruction the notification date was **verified against external sources at fix time** (the maintainer authorised attempting this in-session rather than deferring): the final Rules were notified by MeitY via Gazette Notification G.S.R. 846(E) **dated 13 November 2025** (draft published 3 January 2025), with a three-phase commencement (Data Protection Board provisions on notification; consent-manager provisions around November 2026; the remaining substantive obligations around May 2027), confirmed against two independent legal-firm sources. India is the one jurisdiction absent from the scratch `ref/legislation/` base, so external web verification was the only ground-truth path. The index bullet was reconciled to the annex and the citations register (now mutually consistent across all three surfaces); the index's India table row (:118, "DPDPA 2023 / Rules 2025") carried no date claim and was left unchanged, and no parallel stale "April 2025" occurrence exists elsewhere in the corpus. Per-document Version + Date bumped on the one edited doc ([`privacy/annex-privacy-jurisdiction-index.md`](privacy/annex-privacy-jurisdiction-index.md) `1.0.6` to `1.0.7`); [`taxonomy.yml`](taxonomy.yml) and [`docs/maturity-scorecard.md`](docs/maturity-scorecard.md) regenerated. Closes FR-175 (TODO to DONE), clearing the entire High set FR-168..175. Also batches the #415 `/validate-pr` (0 findings, 1 sub-threshold style advisory not routed) and `/retro` rows. ## 2026-06-27, Library Version 2026.06.373, PR #394

Added an advisory semantic-fit triage tool, [`tools/audit-matrix-semantic-fit.py`](tools/audit-matrix-semantic-fit.py), for the gate-blind "valid code, wrong control" class (a control code that exists in its catalogue, so gates 48/49/54 pass it, but is the wrong control for the row's document). The stdlib-only, recall-oriented tool worklists rows in the compliance matrix ([`compliance/matrix-grc-compliance-alignment.md`](compliance/matrix-grc-compliance-alignment.md)) and in per-document framework-alignment tables that lack any lexical anchor between the document subject and the cited control titles, narrowing the scope for the queued `/matrix-fit` semantic audit ([`TODO.md`](TODO.md) section 4.20, PR B) to adjudicate. It is deliberately NOT a gate: `audit-`-named so the parity and regression machinery does not auto-discover it, never wired into [`tools/run_all_audits.sh`](tools/run_all_audits.sh) or CI, and it always exits 0 (a lexical signal cannot be precision-first for semantic fit, so its output is a worklist, not a verdict). This is the first half of the cadenced-semantic-fit-audit capability; the `/matrix-fit` skill and its cadence wiring follow in PR B. Also batches the clean Sweep 61 records (the loop-break corpus-wide `/validate` over the #390 to #393 deltas, which independently re-verified #392's control-code remediation against the CSA CCM v4.1 ground truth: 0 error, 0 warning, 2 out-of-window notes). Standards-validation discipline for local project: codify how the scratch repo's `ref/standards/` reference base is validated when it informs corpus work, the discipline whose absence let the CCM/AICM-confusion hole (#390) and a class of worker semantic mislabels go uncaught until a manual cross-check surfaced them. Adds a maintainer dev-aid [`tools/verify-reference-modules.py`](tools/verify-reference-modules.py) that confirms the in-repo control-reference modules (which gates 48/49/54 enforce against) match the authoritative scratch source extracts in both directions: `CCM_V41` against the CSA CCM v4.1.0 catalogue CSV (207 codes), `AICM_V11` against the AICM v1.1.0 catalogue CSV (247 codes), and the NIST CSF 2.0 categories against the CSWP-29 full-text extract (22 categories). It is a dev-aid, not a CI gate (the scratch source is absent in CI), named `verify-*` not `lint-*` so the gate machinery does not auto-discover it, and it skips cleanly when the scratch base is unavailable. Codifies the **standards-validation discipline** in the [`multi-session-orchestration`](.working/multi-session-orchestration.md) runbook section 6: (1) code-set parity via the new aid, (2) validate a mapping's semantic fit against the source control *title*, not the code number (code existence is necessary but not sufficient: a valid code can be the wrong control), (3) CCM and AICM are distinct catalogues, never confuse them. Adds two worker-brief guard rails ([`worker-brief-template.md`](.working/worker-brief-template.md) DO rails 9 and 10) for the same two failure classes. ## 2026-06-27, Library Version 2026.06.369, PR #390

Audit-tooling hardening for local project: close a CCM/AICM catalogue-confusion hole in the compliance-matrix control-code gate (gate 49). The matrix's "CSA CCM v4.1" column was validated only by the corpus-wide CSA citation gate (gate 48), which checks a matrix token against the AICM-wins union and so would pass an AICM-only code (for example an `MDS-` Model Security code, an AICM v1.1 domain that CCM v4.1 does not have) sitting in a column labelled CCM v4.1. Gate 49 now validates that column for CCM v4.1.0 catalogue membership and flags an AICM-only identifier as a CCM/AICM confusion, complementary to gate 48 (which keeps CCM/AICM title accuracy). Splits the blended `VALID_DOMAINS` in [`tools/ccm_aicm_reference.py`](tools/ccm_aicm_reference.py) into per-catalogue `CCM_DOMAINS` (17) and `AICM_DOMAINS` (18) with `is_ccm_v41` / `is_aicm` / `is_aicm_only` helpers, so a caller can enforce catalogue discipline rather than relying on the union. Adds three regression fixtures (an AICM-only code, an unknown code, a valid-code false-positive guard) replacing the prior "CCM not policed here" test, and updates the audit-programme spec sections 5 and 6 gate-49 narrative. The crib and every code used were cross-validated against the scratch repo's `ref/standards/` source extracts (the in-repo CCM module matches the CSA CCM v4.1.0 catalogue CSV exactly at 207 codes; the NIST CSF module matches CSWP-29 at 22 categories). Also batches the clean **Sweep 60** `/validate` history row in [`.working/validate-sweeps/history.md`](.working/validate-sweeps/history.md) (the #389 loop-break compensating control over the #387/#388/#389 deltas; 0 findings across all three subagents; no asserted-expectations contradiction). ## 2026-06-26, Library Version 2026.06.354, PR #375

`.claude/` operating-procedure change for local project: codified the **wind-down decision framework** in [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](.claude/CLAUDE.md) (a new section after the attended-autonomous operating mode). It converts the session-ending handoff from a silent unilateral call into a surfaced decision: whenever the assistant concludes a handoff is right, it presents its justification, a per-PR likelihood-of-success assessment of the pending next-five PRs (anchored to objective tractability signals, not a subjective read), and named options (A handoff / B recommended additional PRs / C higher-risk order / D a deliberate Ulysses-pact impulse-check that triggers an immediate handoff if chosen). The decision uses the same roughly-2-minute graceful-degradation timer as the attended-autonomous mechanism and defaults to handoff on no answer; Quality > Speed stays the tiebreaker and options B/C are bounded ("one more, re-assess, repeat", full per-PR `/validate-pr` + `/retro` each). Cross-referenced from the [`.working/session-handoff.md`](.working/session-handoff.md) standing-disciplines bullet. Also batches the PR #374 `/validate-pr` (0 findings) + `/retro` rows (the latter surfaced an update-one-of-a-pair pattern candidate). ## 2026-06-26, Library Version 2026.06.349, PR #370

Integrity-tooling track (PR 1 of 3, the gate-49 extension / DD-12 migration): added [`tools/lint-document-control-codes.py`](tools/lint-document-control-codes.py), a corpus-wide sibling of gate 49 ([`tools/lint-matrix-control-codes.py`](tools/lint-matrix-control-codes.py)) that validates NIST CSF 2.0 control codes wherever they appear in any corpus document's framework-reference or crosswalk tables, not only the central compliance matrix. It reuses the authoritative 22-Category CSF 2.0 set and the CSF-1.1 relocation map in [`tools/nist_csf_reference.py`](tools/nist_csf_reference.py), recognises both the framework-as-row and framework-as-column table shapes, strips subcategory suffixes (`DE.CM-7` to `DE.CM`) and validates at the Category level, and is precision-first: it extracts codes only from the code cell of a framework-row (never trailing notes cells) and only from the NIST column of a column-table, so a CSF-1.1 code inside a legitimate rename note is not a false positive. Scoped to NIST CSF 2.0 (per-document ISO Annex A deferred to a follow-up); excludes the central matrix (gate 49's target) and the [`dev-security/claude-rules/`](dev-security/claude-rules/README.md) pack subtree. The scanner is shipped as a discovery tool, not yet wired as an audit gate: run corpus-wide it reports the authoritative DD-12 carrier inventory (5 CSF-1.1-era codes across 3 files: [`risk/standard-third-party-and-supply-chain-risk.md`](risk/standard-third-party-and-supply-chain-risk.md):230 `ID.SC`; [`operations/procedure-security-monitoring-and-alert-management.md`](operations/procedure-security-monitoring-and-alert-management.md):333/336/337 `RS.RP`/`DE.DP`/`DE.DP`; [`compliance/procedure-capa.md`](compliance/procedure-capa.md):475 `RC.IM`), so wiring it as a gate now would fail until those carriers migrate (PR 2 of the track); the gate wiring lands in PR 3 once the corpus is clean. A `DocumentControlCodeTests` regression class in [`tests/test_linters.py`](tests/test_linters.py) covers both table shapes, the subcategory-strip, the notes-cell precision guard, the NIST-SP-row non-match, and valid/unknown-category cases. Also batches the Sweep 54 loop-break `/validate` history row (the `/resume` compensating control for session-closing handoff PR #369, covering the #366/#367/#368/#369 deltas; full A/B/C dispatch, 0 findings clean, no asserted-expectations contradiction) and advances the TODO sweep cursor to Sweep 54. Integrity-tooling aid closing TODO §4.14 (CHANGELOG-hygiene first-commit pre-flight): added [`tools/preflight-changelog.py`](tools/preflight-changelog.py), a commit-gating helper run as `python3 tools/preflight-changelog.py && git commit ...` that exits non-zero when the *added* lines of the root [`CHANGELOG.md`](CHANGELOG.md) or its detailed mirror carry an em-dash or en-dash in prose (code spans stripped first, matching gate 51) or a path-shaped backtick code span not wrapped in a markdown link (mirroring [`tools/lint-changelog-link-coverage.py`](tools/lint-changelog-link-coverage.py)). Scoped to added lines so historical entries never false-alarm. It is the durable commit-gating form the §4.14 escalation called for (a check that gates the commit, not one that merely reports alongside an unconditional `&& git commit`); a standalone helper rather than a pre-commit hook because no `.git/hooks/pre-commit` fires on commits in this environment (verified before building). Documented in a [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](.claude/CLAUDE.md) close-out-checklist bullet. It is a developer aid, not a new audit gate; the authoritative gates (D3, gate 51, link-coverage) remain in CI. ## 2026-06-26, Library Version 2026.06.345, PR #366

Integrity-tooling delta gate closing TODO §4.17 (the Version-Date co-bump check): added **delta gate D4 (per-PR Version-Date co-bump)**, [`tools/check-date-cobump-on-pr.py`](tools/check-date-cobump-on-pr.py), a PR-only check (sibling to D1/D2/D3) that fails when a PR bumps a versioned document's `**Version:**` field but leaves its `**Date:**` field not equal to the date of the bump commit (UTC). It closes the residue that gates 40 (corpus version-bump-recency) and 31 (document-date-staleness) leave open: gate 40 is silent on the Date, and gate 31 tolerates a 1-day lag, so a Version bump whose Date was left one day stale passes (the recurring sub-shape `/retro` confirmed at PR #325 and PR #352). It is delta-scoped rather than a HEAD-state gate-40 extension because prototyping showed a HEAD-state form has a roughly 78-document historical false-positive surface (a single 2026-05-31 mass commit accounts for dozens), whereas the delta form sees only the PR diff and so has none; comparing against the bump commit's date also keeps it false-positive-free for same-day sequential PRs. Wired into [`.github/workflows/quality.yml`](.github/workflows/quality.yml), the pre-push runner [`tools/run-pr-time-checks.sh`](tools/run-pr-time-checks.sh), and [`governance/specification-audit-programme.md`](governance/specification-audit-programme.md) §6.1 (`1.16.9` to `1.16.10`), with a `DateCobumpOnPrTests` regression class in [`tests/test_linters.py`](tests/test_linters.py). Also batches the **Sweep 53** loop-break `/validate` history row and per-iteration detail file (the `/resume` compensating control for session-closing handoff PRs #363 and #365, covering the #362/#363/#364/#365 deltas; full A/B/C dispatch, 1 out-of-window note cross-referenced into DD-12, 0 in-window). Library `2026.06.344` to `2026.06.345`; audit-programme spec `1.16.9` to `1.16.10`; README `1.9.215` to `1.9.216`.

## 2026-06-26, Library Version 2026.06.341, PR #362

Integrity-tooling gate closing the TODO P2 directional-dependency gate: added **gate 53 (corpus-to-project directional-dependency)**, [`tools/lint-directional-dependency.py`](tools/lint-directional-dependency.py), the mechanical backstop for the project-governance-separation spec §4 one-way dependency rule. It flags any deliverable-corpus document that contains a markdown link whose resolved target is inside [`.project-governance/`](.project-governance/README.md) (a corpus-to-project link inverts the dependency; project governance depends on the corpus, never the reverse); it is the §4 counterpart to gate 52's §7.4 scan-scope parity, the two together making the separation spec's dependency invariants standing mechanical checks rather than migration-discipline conventions. The deliverable-corpus scan set is derived from [`tools/lint_common.py`](tools/lint_common.py) `AUDITED_DOMAIN_DIRS` minus `.project-governance` plus the root deliverable specifications, so a future audited domain propagates from one place and the gate does not itself hardcode the domain run gate 52 forbids; the non-deliverable surfaces §4 permits to link into the directory (the pack under [`dev-security/claude-rules/`](dev-security/claude-rules/README.md), the backlog [`TODO.md`](TODO.md), the root [`CHANGELOG.md`](CHANGELOG.md), the generated indexes, the `.working/` and `.claude/` trees) are out of scope. Detection mirrors the broken-link checker (gate 3): fenced blocks and external targets are skipped, and a target is resolved relative to its source before the `.project-governance` path-component test, so every relative shape is caught. The corpus is clean on landing (no deliverable document links into the directory; the migration that created it severed every such link in PR #336). Wired into all four surfaces with a `DirectionalDependencyTests` regression class; the §7.3 narrative is rewritten from "queued" to built, and the §4 cross-reference updated. Also batches the **Sweep 52** loop-break `/validate` history row (the #361 compensating control over the #359/#360/#361 deltas, 0 findings clean). Library `2026.06.340` to `2026.06.341`; pack `1.49.16` to `1.49.17`; audit-programme spec `1.16.8` to `1.16.9`; project-governance-separation spec `1.0.3` to `1.0.4`; README `1.9.211` to `1.9.212`.

## 2026-06-26, Library Version 2026.06.336, PR #357

Added **gate 51 (working-tree prose-hygiene)** to the audit programme: [`tools/lint-working-prose-hygiene.py`](tools/lint-working-prose-hygiene.py) forbids em-dashes and en-dashes in the prose of the `.working/` maintainer tree (the tree every other content linter exempts) while allowing them inside inline code spans and fenced code blocks, so the 2026-06-26 `.working/` em-dash conformance (#353) cannot silently regress. Wired into all four audit surfaces ([`tools/run_all_audits.sh`](tools/run_all_audits.sh), [`.github/workflows/quality.yml`](.github/workflows/quality.yml), [`.pre-commit-config.yaml`](.pre-commit-config.yaml), and [`governance/specification-audit-programme.md`](governance/specification-audit-programme.md) §6 as row 51) with a `WorkingProseHygieneTests` regression class in [`tests/test_linters.py`](tests/test_linters.py); the gate-39-blind growth-narrative word-form in [`dev-security/claude-rules/skills/guardrail-review/SKILL.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/skills/guardrail-review/SKILL.md) bumped from "fifty" to "fifty-one". Implementation note: the inline-code-span stripper uses the standard CommonMark code-span regex (a run of N backticks, content, a closing run of N) rather than a naive single-backtick strip, which mis-pairs spans whose content contains backticks (the self-referential handoff line that quoted the design was exactly such a case, and was rephrased). Also batches the **Sweep 50** loop-break `/validate` history row (the deferred #354/#356 compensating control over the #352 to #356 deltas; 0 findings, corpus byte-identical to the Sweep-48/49 state). Audit programme 50 to 51 gates; spec `1.16.6` to `1.16.7`; pack `1.49.14` to `1.49.15`; Library `2026.06.335` to `2026.06.336`; README `1.9.206` to `1.9.207`.

## 2026-06-25, Library Version 2026.06.322, PR #343

**Gate 50 (Bookkeeping-parity audit) added to the audit programme** ([`tools/lint-bookkeeping-parity.py`](tools/lint-bookkeeping-parity.py)), the §4.11 worker-provenance / bookkeeping-parity gate family member. It is the honest mechanical backstop for the per-PR QA cadence and the backlog-to-DONE rotation discipline: it enforces the PRESENCE of the bookkeeping records the process mandates, not their semantic correctness. Check 1 (QA-cadence parity) derives the merged-PR list from the `## ... PR #N` headers in [`CHANGELOG.md`](CHANGELOG.md) and, for each PR in `[INCEPTION=329, max(PR))`, requires a row in [`.working/validate-pr/history.md`](.working/validate-pr/history.md) and (for substantive PRs) [`.working/improvement-log.md`](.working/improvement-log.md), with the highest-PR batch-lag exemption, the session-closing-handoff-PR exemption (detected by the `SKIPPED`/`handoff-PR exception` Findings cell), the subsumption/maintainer-exception row (the #328 instance), and a `KNOWN_HANDOFF_NO_ROW` allowlist (`#300`/`#322`/`#334`) for handoff PRs merged before the exemption-row convention. Check 2 (TODO/DONE rotation parity) is precision-first / FP-free: it flags only unambiguous self-completion markers on a backlog bullet (uppercase `SHIPPED in #N`/`DONE in #N`, `Status: completed|done|shipped`, a `[done]`/`[shipped]`/`[x]` checkbox/suffix, or a leading strikethrough), with code-span and bullet-start precision so the open FR-167 batch-sequence strikethrough and the maintenance-note convention reference are not flagged. Check 3 (worker-provenance attestation) is a documented dormant stub until the worker-delivered marking convention and the external-collaborator primitive exist. Wired into all four audit surfaces (gate count **49 to 50**) with a 13-case regression class in [`tests/test_linters.py`](tests/test_linters.py); modelled on gate 45 ([`tools/lint-todo-staleness.py`](tools/lint-todo-staleness.py)) and deliberately kept out of the pre-push history-aware runner (it parses committed content, not the commit graph, so [`tools/run_all_audits.sh`](tools/run_all_audits.sh) already covers it pre-push). Also corrects the [`dev-security/claude-rules/skills/guardrail-review/SKILL.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/skills/guardrail-review/SKILL.md) growth-narrative word-form "a dozen gates to forty-nine" to "fifty" (gate-39-blind, fixed proactively rather than left for the next sweep; pack `1.49.11` to `1.49.12`), and queues [`TODO.md`](TODO.md) §4.13 (a maintainer-requested `/guardrails` coherence review of the 50-gate inventory, maintainer-directed to run immediately upon the gate-50 addition). Batches the zero-finding **Sweep 47** `/validate` history row (the #342 loop-break compensating control, clean). [`governance/specification-audit-programme.md`](governance/specification-audit-programme.md) `1.16.5` to `1.16.6`; taxonomy and scorecard regenerated. ## 2026-06-24, Library Version 2026.06.304, PR #325

Added **gate 49 (Matrix control-code validity audit)** to the audit programme: a new linter [`tools/lint-matrix-control-codes.py`](tools/lint-matrix-control-codes.py) that validates the framework-control codes in [`compliance/matrix-grc-compliance-alignment.md`](compliance/matrix-grc-compliance-alignment.md) for the columns no existing gate covers. It checks every ISO 27001:2022 column token is a real Annex A control code (`A.5`-`A.8` within each theme's count: 37/8/14/34, 93 total) or a management-system clause (`§4`-`§10`), and every NIST CSF 2.0 token is well-formed (`FUNCTION.CATEGORY` with a CSF 2.0 Core Function prefix). Scope is deliberately bounded (the §4.6a maintainer-asked item): the CSA CCM column is already validated corpus-wide by gate 48 (reused, not duplicated); NIST category-level membership is deferred (the authoritative CSF 2.0 category set is not yet encoded; tracked as the §4.6a follow-up, for which the maintainer supplied NIST CSWP.29); and the customs/trade columns (CTPAT/PIP/BASC/WCO SAFE/AEO-S) are free-text with no closed code set. ## 2026-06-24, Library Version 2026.06.303, PR #324

`.claude/` + `.working/` process codification for local project: codified the maintainer-accepted **handoff asserted-expectations** convention. A session-closing handoff now records, scoped to the surfaces it actually verified or covered with a formal QA pass, what it asserts clean (plus a `green-at-<sha>` mechanical-baseline line), and the next `/resume`'s corpus-wide `/validate` cross-checks its findings against those claims: a contradiction of a claimed-clean touched surface reads as a genuine miss rather than an ordinary out-of-window finding. This is the cheap loop-break signal that replaces a wasteful second close-time `/validate` (rejected because the corpus is byte-identical across the boundary, so two non-deterministic subagent runs would differ only by sampling variance; the one deterministic close-vs-start diff worth keeping is the mechanical `green-at-<sha>`, already re-checked at `/resume`). Surfaces: a new `## Asserted expectations` section + the `green-at-<sha>` line in [`.working/session-handoff.md`](.working/session-handoff.md); PR-workflow step 5c, the close-out checklist, and the two handoff mechanisms in [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](.claude/CLAUDE.md); steps 3 and 5 of [`.claude/commands/resume.md`](.claude/commands/resume.md). Also carries the batched #323 `/validate-pr` (0 findings) and `/retro` (post-Version-bump artefact-regen pattern, third instance) register rows. No corpus-content change. Library `2026.06.302` to `2026.06.303`; README `1.9.173` to `1.9.174`.

## 2026-06-24, Library Version 2026.06.300, PR #321

**FR-140: resolve the adopter starter-set divergence.** The library presented four different "starter set" sizes across its adopter on-ramps (a 6-artefact Day-1 floor, a 15-document Tier 1 set, a ~25-document sector path, and a ~37-artefact README "Core reference set"), and, more substantively, the 6-artefact Day-1 floor named the acceptable-use and identity-and-access-management policies as non-negotiable while the *larger* 15-document Tier 1 set omitted both, so the floor was not a subset of Tier 1. Per maintainer decision (Option A), [`docs/adopter-guide.md`](docs/adopter-guide.md) Tier 1 gains [`security/policy-acceptable-use.md`](security/policy-acceptable-use.md) and [`security/policy-identity-and-access-management.md`](security/policy-identity-and-access-management.md) (15 → 17 documents), making the Day-1 floor a strict subset; the `15`→`17` count and the floor/Tier-1 reconciliation prose are harmonized across [`docs/template-quickstart.md`](docs/template-quickstart.md), [`docs/adopter-guide.md`](docs/adopter-guide.md), and [`docs/decision-tree.md`](docs/decision-tree.md); and [`README.md`](README.md)'s "Core reference set" is reframed as the curated foundational *catalogue* an adopter grows toward (cross-referenced to the quickstart/adopter-guide starting points) rather than a competing "authoritative starter set". To make the Day-1 floor a strict subset of the catalogue too, the README core reference set gains the two floor artefacts it was missing, [`security/policy-acceptable-use.md`](security/policy-acceptable-use.md) and [`security/procedure-security-incident-response.md`](security/procedure-security-incident-response.md) (it already carried the other four). Closes FR-140. Also bundles, per recursion-avoidance, the #320 `/validate-pr` + `/retro` register rows and the one out-of-window finding that sweep surfaced: [`privacy/annex-privacy-jurisdiction-index.md`](privacy/annex-privacy-jurisdiction-index.md):133's "2026 Update summary" said Bill C-27 "Remained under parliamentary study as of early 2026", corrected to the corpus consensus (lapsed at the 2025-01-06 prorogation; PIPEDA in force). Taxonomy and scorecard regenerated. Library `2026.06.298` to `2026.06.300`; README `1.9.169` to `1.9.171`. See [`.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md`](.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md) for the full per-file detail and the discipline observation.

## 2026-06-24, Library Version 2026.06.298, PR #320

**DD-8: scrub the live-regime sense of CPPA to PIPEDA across the corpus.** The Consumer Privacy Protection Act (CPPA, Part 1 of Canada's Bill C-27) never became law (the bill lapsed at the 2025-01-06 prorogation); PIPEDA remains the in-force Canadian federal private-sector privacy regime. This sweep corrects the corpus's residual treatment of CPPA as a current/applicable regime, a **full principled scrub** (maintainer-chosen) across **29 documents**: bare `CPPA` in a live-applicable framework list became `PIPEDA` (e.g. [`security/procedure-security-incident-response.md`](security/procedure-security-incident-response.md) §6 notification table + §6.2 heading, [`risk/standard-enterprise-risk-management.md`](risk/standard-enterprise-risk-management.md), [`security/standard-logging-and-monitoring.md`](security/standard-logging-and-monitoring.md), [`supply-chain/procedure-supplier-due-diligence.md`](supply-chain/procedure-supplier-due-diligence.md)); `PIPEDA / CPPA` pairs dropped the redundant live-CPPA (the sector annexes, [`privacy/register-cross-border-data-flow.md`](privacy/register-cross-border-data-flow.md), [`privacy/template-joint-controller-arrangement.md`](privacy/template-joint-controller-arrangement.md)); the three [`governance/register-document-index-and-classification.md`](governance/register-document-index-and-classification.md) Frameworks tags for the docs PR #264 already body-scrubbed were reconciled to PIPEDA; CPPA-specific content was qualified rather than replaced ([`risk/annex-ai-risk-methodology.md`](risk/annex-ai-risk-methodology.md) algorithmic-transparency row to `CPPA (Canada, proposed)`; [`privacy/annex-privacy-jurisdiction-index.md`](privacy/annex-privacy-jurisdiction-index.md) coverage row to `CPPA (pending)`); and a factual error in [`governance/register-glossary.md`](governance/register-glossary.md) ("PIPEDA being superseded by CPPA") was fixed. **Preserved**: the distinct California Privacy Protection Agency (CPPA) sense in [`privacy/jurisdictions/annex-privacy-united-states.md`](privacy/jurisdictions/annex-privacy-united-states.md), and every mention already qualified pending/proposed/lapsed (the Canada annex, the privacy crosswalk rows, [`governance/register-canonical-citations.md`](governance/register-canonical-citations.md)). Closes DD-8 (surfaced by PR #264 / FR-138, which deferred the broader sweep). Also carries the `/resume` corpus-wide **Sweep 40** history row and detail file ([`.working/validate-sweeps/2026-06-24-sweep40-iter1.md`](.working/validate-sweeps/2026-06-24-sweep40-iter1.md)): 1 in-window note on [`dev-security/claude-rules/languages/go.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/languages/go.md) TLS-field precision (`PreferServerCipherSuites` is deprecated and ignored in current Go, not "TLS 1.2 and below" as the #318 comment grouped it), which the maintainer chose to **fold into this PR** rather than defer: the comment is reworded so `CipherSuites` (TLS-1.2-scoped) and `PreferServerCipherSuites` (deprecated/ignored) are described distinctly; the #318 load-bearing TLS-1.3 claim is unchanged. Taxonomy and scorecard regenerated. Library `2026.06.297` to `2026.06.298`; pack `1.49.8` to `1.49.9` (the go.md fold-in); README `1.9.168` to `1.9.169`. ## 2026-06-24, Library Version 2026.06.292, PR #314

**New [`governance/specification-project-governance-separation.md`](governance/specification-project-governance-separation.md): a process separating corpus/library governance from project governance.** Adds a Specification (v1.0.1) drawing the boundary between the governance content the library publishes as its deliverable (corpus/library governance) and the operational records of running this project (project governance), which had both accumulated in `governance/`. The criterion is reusable-pattern-versus-operational-instance: a specification, procedure, or template of a process is a reusable pattern (corpus); the filled-in record of having executed that process on this corpus is an operational instance (project). The boundary is kept clean by a one-way dependency rule (project governance may cite corpus; corpus must not cite project governance), which makes the corpus document index corpus-only and turns any migration into citation surgery rather than a file move. Project-governance artefacts will live in a new top-level `.project-governance/` directory (dot-prefixed like `.working/` and `.claude/`, but NOT exempt: fully audited, with adopter-facing generator and index inclusion the only sweep behaviour that changes). The spec classifies all 40 current `governance/` artefacts (§5): 33 stay corpus (including this spec and, by maintainer decision 2026-06-24, [`register-canonical-citations.md`](governance/register-canonical-citations.md) as the reusable citation reference whose verification log is the operational instance), 6 (the citation-verification campaign cluster) migrate in Phase 1, and 2 ([`register-coverage-gaps.md`](governance/register-coverage-gaps.md), [`register-document-review-schedule.md`](governance/register-document-review-schedule.md)) are deferred to per-artefact later decisions. This closes the deferred backlog item R2 by principle (the citation-verification cluster is project governance, so it migrates in Phase 1) and records why R1 was correctly closed won't-move (scanner-private config already in [`tools/`](tools/)). No files move in this PR; Phase 1 migration, the queued directional-dependency gate (§7.3), and the deferred classifications are queued in [`TODO.md`](TODO.md). Wired into [`governance/README.md`](governance/README.md) and the corpus document index; taxonomy, portal, and scorecard regenerated. Carries the batched #313 `/validate-pr` (0 findings) and `/retro` rows. Library `2026.06.291` to `2026.06.292`; README `1.9.162` to `1.9.163`. See [`.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md`](.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md) for detail.

## 2026-06-24, Library Version 2026.06.288, PR #310

The corpus had three divergences from that canon: the supplier concentration register used the old "Rare/Unlikely/Possible/Likely/Almost Certain" likelihood labels and "Severe" for impact-5; the operational-risk-register template used "Moderate" where the canonical likelihood label is "Medium" and "Severe" for impact-5; and the risk-assessment procedure and the enterprise-risk-register template labelled impact-5 "Critical", which collides with the canonical rating-top "Critical" (17-25). The rating-top "Critical" (score 17-25) is preserved in every document (the impact-5-versus-rating "Critical" conflation is the precise thing resolved); the concentration register's separate qualitative "Overall residual risk" descriptor (Negligible/Low/Moderate/High/Unacceptable) is a doc-specific output scale, not the 4-band rating, and was left intact. ## 2026-06-24, Library Version 2026.06.287, PR #309

**S5: gate 48 (CSA CCM/AICM citation-accuracy) gains a bare-domain-code check (Check 4).** Closes the TODO S5 item (surfaced by Sweep 36, where PR #298's reconciliation left bare domain-code residuals that the token-scoped gate could not see and the orchestrator grep had to catch). [`tools/lint-ccm-aicm-citations.py`](tools/lint-ccm-aicm-citations.py) now flags a bare superseded or fabricated CCM domain code (one with no `<DOMAIN>-<NN>` suffix, in a framework family list, a domain-keyed crosswalk row, or a glossary-style entry) when the line either names the matrices (CCM / CSA / Cloud Controls Matrix / AICM) or sits under a CCM/AICM section heading, and is not a historical rename-note. The design is precision-first: the token boundary excludes `.NET`, the corpus-internal `AI-GOV` / `MODEL-GOV` identifiers, and the `<CODE>-<NN>` control tokens; the CCM-context requirement excludes currency `AUD` and "government" prose; a rename-note exemption (`renamed` / `superseded` / `corrected` and similar) clears the glossary I&S rename-note and the pack-README version-history rows; and [`TODO.md`](TODO.md) is added to the gate's meta-exempt set (it names the codes when describing the gate's own follow-up items). The recall limit is documented: a bad code in a multi-framework mapping table where the CCM column is unlabelled on the row and the section heading is generic is not caught (the apply-time grep and the periodic sweep cover that tail). Four regression cases added to [`tests/test_linters.py`](tests/test_linters.py) (two fire cases for the family-list and CCM-section shapes, two false-positive guards for the rename-note and the `.NET`/currency cases); gate 48 stays clean on the corpus (376 files; TODO now exempt). Still 48 gates, no parity change; completes the gate-48 enhancement pair with S4 (#308). Carries the batched #308 `/validate-pr` (0 in-window findings, 1 self-resolved out-of-window note) and `/retro` records. Library `2026.06.286` to `2026.06.287`; README `1.9.157` to `1.9.158`. See [`.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md`](.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md) for detail.

## 2026-06-24, Library Version 2026.06.286, PR #308

**S4: gate 48 (CSA CCM/AICM citation-accuracy) gains a section-aware, cross-catalogue title check.** Closes the TODO S4 item (surfaced by PR #299's `/validate-pr`). [`tools/lint-ccm-aicm-citations.py`](tools/lint-ccm-aicm-citations.py)'s control-listing title check is now **section-aware**: a row under a `## CSA CCM ...` heading is checked against the CCM v4.1.0 title, one under an `## AICM ...` heading against the AICM v1.1.0 title, and one under neither against the AICM-wins union (the prior behaviour, preserved for unscoped tables). A new **cross-catalogue check** flags the gate-escaping class the union check is blind to: a small set of controls share a code across both matrices but carry titles differing by a distinctive content word (I&S-07 is "Migration to Cloud Environments" in CCM v4.1.0 but "Migration to Hosted Environments" in AICM v1.1.0), and because the two titles share most content words the conservative content-word check never fires on the mix-up. The new check fails a row under a CCM section that carries the AICM variant's distinctive word (and none of the CCM variant's), and vice versa; this is exactly the I&S-07 confusion that PR #299's `/validate-pr` had to catch by hand. Controls differing only by punctuation (IAM-11's "Customers" vs "Customers'") have no distinctive content word and are intentionally not policed, consistent with the gate's tolerance of localized wording. Two regression cases added to [`tests/test_linters.py`](tests/test_linters.py) (the cross-catalogue fail case plus a false-positive guard for the correct title); gate 48 stays clean on the corpus (still 48 gates, no parity change, an enhancement to the existing gate). Carries the batched #307 `/validate-pr` (0 findings, clean) and `/retro` records. Library `2026.06.285` to `2026.06.286`; README `1.9.156` to `1.9.157`. See [`.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md`](.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md) for detail.

## 2026-06-23, Library Version 2026.06.256, PR #278

**DD-1: add PR-time delta gate D3 so new CHANGELOG entries follow the no-dash prose convention, leaving history untouched.** Deferred decision DD-1 asked whether to bring the root [`CHANGELOG.md`](CHANGELOG.md) under the em-dash and en-dash prohibition that [`tools/lint-language.py`](tools/lint-language.py) enforces on the corpus. The CHANGELOG sits outside that whole-file linter because its append-only history holds roughly 130 dashes accumulated before the convention applied, and rewriting historical entries would churn the record and risk altering past entries' meaning. The maintainer chose the new-entries-only resolution: a PR-time delta gate (D3, [`tools/check-changelog-dash-on-pr.py`](tools/check-changelog-dash-on-pr.py)) that inspects only the CHANGELOG lines a PR adds and fails on any em dash or en dash, so future entries follow the convention while history stays intact. Wired into the local PR-time runner [`tools/run-pr-time-checks.sh`](tools/run-pr-time-checks.sh), CI ([`.github/workflows/quality.yml`](.github/workflows/quality.yml), PR-only, alongside D1 and D2), and the audit-programme spec [`governance/specification-audit-programme.md`](governance/specification-audit-programme.md) section 6.1 (`1.15.0 → 1.16.0`). The scope was re-confirmed with the maintainer at action time after investigation found roughly 130 dashes (not the approximately five the decision assumed), making a whole-file rewrite disproportionate. Also carries the batched PR #277 `/validate-pr` (0 findings) and `/retro` rows. Library `2026.06.255 → 2026.06.256`; README `1.9.126 → 1.9.127`. See [`.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md`](.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md) for detail.

## 2026-06-23, Library Version 2026.06.250, PR #272

**FR-166: corpus listing-surface completeness gate + authoring-time sweep tool.** Governance work must be meticulous, so when a new document is added, every surface that should list it must be updated. This PR adds the mechanism. The new **gate 47** ([`tools/lint-listing-surface-completeness.py`](tools/lint-listing-surface-completeness.py)) enforces completeness for the MECHANICAL listing surfaces against the canonical active-document set in [`taxonomy.yml`](taxonomy.yml): the document-index register ([`governance/register-document-index-and-classification.md`](governance/register-document-index-and-classification.md)) must list every domain-prefixed active document, and each domain README must reference every active document in its own domain. Root-level meta-specifications (`specification-*.md`) are exempt by a documented rule (the register is organized by domain and has never indexed them). The new authoring helper [`tools/suggest-listing-surfaces.py`](tools/suggest-listing-surfaces.py) `<doc>` reports, for a new document, the MECHANICAL surfaces (present/missing) plus a ranked high-recall list of SEMANTIC candidates (the framework matrices and crosswalks, the glossary, the Related Documents field) for a human to ratify. Honest contract per `gate-discipline`: MECHANICAL surfaces are hard-gated; the relevance-based SEMANTIC surfaces are NOT gated (a noisy completeness gate over a judgment-based surface would erode gate-discipline), they get suggestions and a `/validate` Subagent B coverage-drift check instead. Wired across all four audit-programme surfaces (workflow, runner, pre-commit, spec §6) with a regression fixture; the gate count moves 46 → 47. The corpus is already complete (the gate passes at HEAD); the only register gap measured (the two root meta-specs) is the documented exemption. Also wires the helper into the new-document procedure ([`specification-ingestion.md`](specification-ingestion.md) checklist item 12) and adds the SEMANTIC coverage-drift check to the [`validation-sweep`](dev-security/claude-rules/skills/validation-sweep/SKILL.md) SKILL's Subagent B scope. Carries the batched PR #271 `/validate-pr` (0 findings) + `/retro` rows. Per-doc: audit-programme spec `1.14.2 → 1.15.0`, ingestion spec `1.7.2 → 1.7.3`; pack `1.49.2 → 1.49.3`; library `2026.06.249 → 2026.06.250`; README `1.9.120 → 1.9.121`. See [`.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md`](.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md) for detail.

## 2026-06-23, Library Version 2026.06.249, PR #271

**Sweep 28 (`/validate`) close-out: fix an in-window DR backup-cadence contradiction surfaced by the session-resume sweep.** The `/resume` compensating-control corpus-wide `/validate` (the standing control for the session-closing handoff PR #270, which skips its trailing `/validate-pr`) ran a full three-subagent dispatch over the whole corpus + the #259-#270 window. FR-139 fixed Tier 1's cadence but, in rewriting the gap clause to bind Tier 2 explicitly to 4 hours, left Tier 2 on the old "daily" cadence. Fixed here: the cadence clause now reads "backups at least every 4 hours for Tier 2's 4-hour RPO, and at least daily backups for Tier 3 and Tier 4" — consistent with the gap clause, the RTO/RPO targets table, and the locked FR-139 principle (cadence must meet RPO), so no new authorial decision (the binding 4-hour gap requirement was already present at :99); per-doc version `1.3.0 → 1.3.1`. ## 2026-06-23, Library Version 2026.06.245, PR #267

**FR-141 (High): remove the invented PIPEDA breach "72-hour target".** Canada's federal `PIPEDA` Breach of Security Safeguards Regulations require reporting to the OPC "as soon as feasible after the organization determines that the breach has occurred" — there is no fixed statutory hour clock, so the "(72-hour target)" annotation was a fabricated deadline (the 72-hour figure is GDPR's, and Quebec Law 25's to the CAI — neither is the PIPEDA federal rule). A bare-token search found the invented annotation at two surfaces (not just the one named in the finding): [`privacy/procedure-data-protection-and-privacy-breach-response.md`](privacy/procedure-data-protection-and-privacy-breach-response.md):171 (`1.4.9 → 1.4.10`; §6.2 jurisdiction table, "Without unreasonable delay (72-hour target)") and [`security/procedure-security-incident-response.md`](security/procedure-security-incident-response.md):176 (`1.3.8 → 1.3.9`; §6 regulatory-notification table, "As soon as feasible (72-hour target)"). Both deadline cells now read "As soon as feasible (no fixed statutory deadline)". The correct 72-hour references elsewhere (GDPR threshold in [`risk/template-risk-appetite-statement.md`](risk/template-risk-appetite-statement.md), Quebec Law 25 to the CAI, Malaysia's PDPC rule) were verified accurate and left unchanged. That §176 cell's separate "CPPA (Canada)" regime label (an FR-138 CPPA-not-in-force issue) is left for the deferred broader-CPPA sweep (logged in [`.working/overnight-pr.md`](.working/overnight-pr.md)); only the FR-141 deadline was changed here. Carries the batched PR #266 `/validate-pr` (0 in-window) + `/retro` rows. Library `2026.06.244 → 2026.06.245`; README `1.9.115 → 1.9.116`. ## 2026-06-23, Library Version 2026.06.243, PR #265

**FR-139 (H[critical]): DR Tier-1 backup cadence aligned to the 1-hour RPO.** [`resilience/plan-it-disaster-recovery.md`](resilience/plan-it-disaster-recovery.md) set a 1-hour RPO for Tier 1 (Mission Critical) in its RTO/RPO targets table, but the backup section mandated "automated daily backups" and a "backup gap not exceeding 24 hours for Tier 1" — both incompatible with a 1-hour RPO. Combined with the rule that "any backup gap exceeding the defined RPO is treated as a P2 risk event", a compliant Tier-1 system would *permanently* sit in P2 escalation, a self-contradiction. Per the maintainer's locked decision (1h RPO binding; the 24h figure is the error and belongs to lower tiers), the backup cadence now requires continuous or near-continuous data protection (journaled/snapshot replication or log shipping) for Tier 1's 1-hour RPO with at least daily backups for Tier 2 and below, and the backup-gap limit is stated per tier (1 hour Tier 1, 4 hours Tier 2; 24h/72h for Tier 3/Tier 4 per the targets table). Per-doc version `1.2.0 → 1.3.0` (minor; the Tier-1 backup-cadence requirement changed substantively). A bare-token search confirms the DR plan is now internally consistent and that [`operations/standard-production-security-requirements.md`](operations/standard-production-security-requirements.md):43 ("RPO 1 hour, RTO 4 hours") corroborates rather than diverges. **This completes the six-item H[critical] locked-criticals batch (FR-134 through FR-139).** Carries the batched PR #264 `/validate-pr` (0 in-window) + `/retro` rows. ## 2026-06-23, Library Version 2026.06.242, PR #264

**FR-138 (H[critical]): scrub CPPA-as-live from the three named privacy documents.** The Consumer Privacy Protection Act (CPPA, Part 1 of Bill C-27) lapsed at the 2025-01-06 prorogation and is not in force ([`privacy/jurisdictions/annex-privacy-canada.md`](privacy/jurisdictions/annex-privacy-canada.md):28 is the canonical statement; PIPEDA remains the federal private-sector law), yet three documents cited CPPA as a live legal basis — with invented-looking section numbers ("CPPA s.63", "s.66", "s.69", "s.67", "s.63(3)") presented as current obligations. Per the maintainer's locked decision, those are replaced with the in-force PIPEDA Schedule 1 basis (the CSA Model Code fair-information principles), with a "CPPA pending reintroduction" note where relevant. [`privacy/procedure-data-subject-rights-management.md`](privacy/procedure-data-subject-rights-management.md) (`1.4.1 → 1.5.0`): the rights table and the summary mapping table now cite PIPEDA Schedule 1 Principle 9 (Individual Access) for access/correction and Principle 3 (Consent, withdrawal) for objection; the erasure and automated-decision rows drop the CPPA citation because PIPEDA provides no such right (GDPR remains the basis); a new "Canadian legal basis" note explains this and that CPPA, if reintroduced, would add disposal and automated-decision rights; the intro, the §4 alignment line, the fees-table row, and the §8.3 heading are de-CPPA'd. [`privacy/procedure-data-protection-and-privacy-breach-response.md`](privacy/procedure-data-protection-and-privacy-breach-response.md) (`1.4.8 → 1.4.9`): the Canada federal breach basis becomes PIPEDA (Breach of Security Safeguards Regulations) with "CPPA pending reintroduction"; the alignment line and the §notification-basis row aligned. **FR-136 (H[critical]): the data-retention schedule is authoritative for log retention.** The logging standard flatly required "a minimum of seven years" for security and audit logs ([`security/standard-logging-and-monitoring.md`](security/standard-logging-and-monitoring.md):92), while the authoritative [`governance/register-data-retention-schedule.md`](governance/register-data-retention-schedule.md) tiers retention by log class (access logs 1 year, privileged-access session logs 2 years, SIEM events 1 year hot + 2 years cold, security incident records 5 years) and the records standard's IT/Security row said "1 to 3 years" — three different answers for the same logs. ## 2026-06-23, Library Version 2026.06.238, PR #260

**FR-134 (H[critical]): one canonical risk-scoring scale across the three risk documents.** The risk standard's §5.2 scoring scale diverged from the canonical risk-assessment procedure: the standard used likelihood labels Rare→Almost Certain and score-to-rating bands `1-5 / 6-10 / 11-15 / 16-25`, while [`risk/procedure-risk-assessment-methodology.md`](risk/procedure-risk-assessment-methodology.md) (the canonical methodology, per maintainer decision) uses Very Low→Very High and bands `1-4 / 5-9 / 10-16 / 17-25`, so the same risk score produced a different rating, review cadence, and escalation depending on which document an assessor read (e.g. a score of 16 was "Critical" under the standard but "High" under the procedure). [`risk/template-enterprise-risk-register.md`](risk/template-enterprise-risk-register.md) (whose bands already agreed and which already cited the procedure) has its stale likelihood labels fixed: the Inherent/Residual Likelihood fields and the 5×5 matrix axis move from Rare→Almost Certain to Very Low→Very High. ## 2026-06-23, Library Version 2026.06.236, PR #258

**Distributes the PRIMORDIAL RULE as the tenth pack governance rule [`project-integrity.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/governance/project-integrity.md)** (pack `1.48.0 → 1.49.0`; closes TODO P4.0). The project's apex `## PRIMORDIAL RULE: PROJECT INTEGRITY` section of [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](.claude/CLAUDE.md) is generalized into a project-agnostic pack governance rule so adopters inherit the lexicographic **Quality > Speed > Cost** ordering and the integrity non-negotiables rather than re-deriving them under pressure. The rule governs a different axis than the other nine: where each of those constrains a specific behaviour, this one fixes the priority ordering that decides which optimization dimension wins when quality, speed, and cost conflict (quality always, then speed, then cost, lexicographically). It re-states the integrity non-negotiables (correctness over apparent completion; no stub/mock/fabrication; no gate suppression; no silent changes; failing states surfaced) as the apex-precedence forms of `gate-discipline`, `evidence-grounded-completion`, and `clarify-before-acting`, and prescribes the self-reminder checkpoint cadence (task start, before persistence, before completion claims, at tension points). Wired across every surface a new governance rule touches: the pack rule file + its [`.claude/rules/governance/project-integrity.md`](.claude/rules/governance/project-integrity.md) byte-identical mirror (gate 37) with the [`tools/lint-claude-rules-sync.py`](tools/lint-claude-rules-sync.py) MIRROR_MAP entry; all three enumeration surfaces (the pack README directory-tree AND its "two areas" prose list, the pack [`CLAUDE.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/CLAUDE.md), the project [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](.claude/CLAUDE.md); gate 41); the rollout-history narrative in both CLAUDE.md files extended to name the tenth rule; the [`tools/lint-collection-enumeration-consistency.py`](tools/lint-collection-enumeration-consistency.py) docstring "nine" → "ten" governance rules; and the project CLAUDE.md PRIMORDIAL RULE forward-reference ("queued as TODO P4.0") now resolved to the shipped rule. ## 2026-06-23, Library Version 2026.06.235, PR #257

**Adds the fifteenth pack skill [`guardrail-review`](dev-security/claude-rules/skills/guardrail-review/SKILL.md) (`/guardrails`)** (pack `1.47.3 → 1.48.0`). The periodic structural-integrity review of the governance machinery itself: the rules, skills, and audit gates, plus their wiring surfaces, reviewed through three lenses the mechanical parity gates cannot apply because they check identity and count, not meaning. **Overlap**: two rules/skills/gates covering the same ground redundantly or contradictorily. **Gap**: a stated discipline no gate enforces, a recurring failure mode (in [`improvement-log.md`](.working/improvement-log.md) / [`hallucination-metrics.md`](.working/hallucination-metrics.md)) no rule names, a rule with no warranted skill, a gate covering one surface while a sibling is ungated. **Drift**: a rule/skill/gate whose meaning diverged across wiring surfaces below the parity gates' resolution (the recurring real instance being a convention revised in a rule but left stale in a one-line enumeration description, which the resume `/validate` of 2026-06-23 caught in the pack README). It is distinct from the content sweeps (`/validate`, `/validate-pr`, which review the corpus) and the trust-recovery suite (`/full-qa`, `/fitness`, which re-examine a window of work): `/guardrails` reviews the apparatus, not the corpus. Cadence: maintainer-triggered plus an auto-prompt after any PR that adds, removes, or renames a rule, skill, or gate. It is a single-pass periodic review (like `/fitness`), not a fix-to-fixed-point loop, because structural findings are maintainer-decision proposals (merge overlapping rules, add a gate, retire a decorative check, reconcile a drifted description), routed tagged `[guardrails]`, tiered by severity, none dropped. Wired across every surface a new skill touches: the SKILL (`derives_from` [`gate-discipline.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/governance/gate-discipline.md)), the [`/guardrails`](.claude/commands/guardrails.md) slash command with step-identifier parity (steps 1-6, gate 44), the [`tools/lint-paired-skill-step-parity.py`](tools/lint-paired-skill-step-parity.py) PAIRS registry, the pack README skills tree (14 to 15 skills, gate 41), bidirectional `## See Also` back-references in `skill-authoring-discipline` and `deep-qa-review`, and a `.working/guardrail-reviews/` record-directory scaffold. Closes the TODO structural-review codification item. Carries the batched PR #256 `/validate-pr` (0 findings) + `/retro` rows. Pack `1.47.3 → 1.48.0`; library `2026.06.234 → 2026.06.235`; README `1.9.105 → 1.9.106`. See [`.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md`](.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md) for detail.

## 2026-06-22, Library Version 2026.06.230, PR #252

**Trust-recovery routing convention revised to severity-tiered** (pack `1.47.0 → 1.47.1`). Per maintainer direction ("routing flag only"), the trust-recovery findings-routing convention changes from "every confirmed finding to a single top-priority tier regardless of severity" to **severity-tiered routing**: High[critical] and High to the top-priority tier (this project: P1), Medium and Low to the next tier (P2). The core invariant is unchanged: nothing the assistant judges trivial is silently dropped (severity governs the destination tier, not whether a finding is surfaced), the maintainer (not the assistant) decides what to defer, and the maintainer-sign-off termination still ends the tier. Propagated in lock-step across every surface that states the convention: the [`trust-recovery-escalation.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/governance/trust-recovery-escalation.md) rule and its [`.claude/rules/governance/trust-recovery-escalation.md`](.claude/rules/governance/trust-recovery-escalation.md) byte-identical mirror; the [`deep-qa-review`](dev-security/claude-rules/skills/deep-qa-review/SKILL.md) SKILL plus the [`/full-qa`](.claude/commands/full-qa.md) command; the [`library-fitness-review`](dev-security/claude-rules/skills/library-fitness-review/SKILL.md) SKILL (new step 5.5 routing-flag) plus the [`/fitness`](.claude/commands/fitness.md) command; and the pack [`CLAUDE.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/CLAUDE.md) plus project [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](.claude/CLAUDE.md) rule-description bullets. The pack [`README.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/README.md) gains a 1.47.1 version-history row; the historical 1.47.0 row is left accurate-to-time. Also carries the deferred PR #251 `/validate-pr` (1 note, reconciled) + `/retro` rows and the routing-surface-list reconciliation per recursion-avoidance. Pack `1.47.0 → 1.47.1`; library `2026.06.229 → 2026.06.230`; README `1.9.100 → 1.9.101`. ## 2026-06-22, Library Version 2026.06.227, PR #249

**Handoff-PR QA loop-break** — closes a recursion in the per-PR QA cadence at session boundaries. A session-closing handoff PR (one whose purpose is to land working-state on `main` as a green merge so the next session resumes from `main`) previously would, per step 5a, run a trailing `/validate-pr` + `/retro`; those produce ledger rows that, per recursion-avoidance, must batch into a *new* PR, whose merge triggers another `/validate-pr` — an unterminating loop, because at a session boundary there is no "next substantive PR" to absorb the rows. This PR codifies the fix the maintainer directed: the session-closing handoff PR is **exempt from the trailing `/validate-pr`/`/retro`**, and the compensating control is that the next session's [`/resume`](.claude/commands/resume.md) runs a full corpus-wide `/validate` as its first task (stronger than the skipped per-PR sweep, since it re-examines the whole corpus). Wired across [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](.claude/CLAUDE.md) (PR-workflow step 5a handoff-PR exception; a new "closing-handoff-PR discipline" point in the session-migration section), [`.claude/commands/resume.md`](.claude/commands/resume.md) (full `/validate` as the first task), and [`.working/session-handoff.md`](.working/session-handoff.md) (how-to-resume step, next-actions item, standing-disciplines exception). The exemption is recorded as a maintainer-authorised standing exception in the [`.working/validate-pr/history.md`](.working/validate-pr/history.md) row for #248+#249 per the no-skip discipline. Follow-ups queued in [`TODO.md`](TODO.md): generalize the carve-out into the pack `validation-sweep-pr-scoped` SKILL + `ai-assistant-workflow-disciplines` rule (so adopters inherit it), the P4.6 gate must design in the handoff-PR exemption, and a new P4.7 scopes an external overnight-driver loop (fresh `claude -p`/SDK session per task-unit reading the handoff) for unattended longer runs. This is itself the session's closing handoff PR. Working-state and config change; the only gated files touched are [`README.md`](README.md) (version lines) and this CHANGELOG. Library `2026.06.226 → 2026.06.227`; README `1.9.97 → 1.9.98`. See [`.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md`](.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md) for detail.

## 2026-06-22, Library Version 2026.06.224, PR #246

**Adds the ninth governance rule [`trust-recovery-escalation.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/governance/trust-recovery-escalation.md) to the dev-security pack** — the second trust-recovery codification PR. The rule names the escalation tier invoked when an AI assistant's discipline failures put a maintainer's confidence in a *window* of work in question: the trigger classes (abbreviated or skipped QA across changes, a skipped verification reaching the shared pipeline, a wrong-cadence automation, an unvalidated inference that cascaded), the two-skill suite (the AI-failure-pattern forensic pass `deep-qa-review` / `/full-qa` first, then the fresh-reader persona pass `library-fitness-review` / `/fitness`), the findings-routing convention (every confirmed finding to the backlog's top priority regardless of severity, apply-time-verified, deduped), and the sign-off discipline (the tier terminates only on explicit maintainer sign-off, not on an empty finding-set). It also carries the full-clone methodology rule. Wired across the three governance-rule enumeration surfaces (pack README directory-tree, pack [`CLAUDE.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/CLAUDE.md), project [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](.claude/CLAUDE.md)) plus the [`.claude/rules/governance/`](.claude/rules/governance/) local mirror and its sync mapping in [`tools/lint-claude-rules-sync.py`](tools/lint-claude-rules-sync.py); the `deep-qa-review` SKILL's two forward references to the rule are now linkified. **Closes FR-164**: the [`tools/lint-collection-enumeration-consistency.py`](tools/lint-collection-enumeration-consistency.py) docstring's stale "seven governance rules" is corrected to "nine". Also bundles the deferred PR #245 `/retro` row and the PR #244 + #245 `/validate-pr` history rows (the #244 row was a recursion-avoidance bookkeeping slip missed in PR #245, caught and corrected here), plus a cosmetic "(TODO P4)" → "(TODO P4.0)" fix in the PRIMORDIAL RULE. Pack `1.46.0 → 1.47.0`; library `2026.06.223 → 2026.06.224`; README `1.9.94 → 1.9.95`. ## 2026-06-22, Library Version 2026.06.223, PR #245

**Adds the PRIMORDIAL RULE: PROJECT INTEGRITY (highest precedence) to [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](.claude/CLAUDE.md).** By maintainer direction, the project now carries an apex rule establishing a lexicographic, absolute priority ordering (Quality > Speed > Cost) with non-negotiable integrity clauses (correctness over apparent completion; no silent changes; no suppression of tests, audit gates, linting, or error handling to force a pass; no fabrication of APIs/citations/behaviour; failing states always surfaced), an escalation directive (halt and surface any forced quality compromise rather than resolve it silently toward speed or cost), and a semantic-checkpoint self-reminder cadence (task start, before commit, before completion claims, at quality/speed/cost tension; the per-file-write and per-N-operations mechanical triggers were dropped as noise by maintainer calibration). The rule consolidates and elevates the integrity disciplines already in the [`dev-security/claude-rules/governance/`](dev-security/claude-rules/governance/) pack (gate-discipline, evidence-grounded-completion, clarify-before-acting, change-tracking) under one priority; it governs optimization-dimension conflicts and is complementary to the existing rule-source layering note. A project-agnostic distributable form is queued as a pack governance rule ([`TODO.md`](TODO.md) P4.0). This PR also carries the deferred PR #244 `/retro` row. Working-state / config change; no adopter-facing corpus content changed. Library `2026.06.222 → 2026.06.223`; README `1.9.93 → 1.9.94`. See [`.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md`](.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md) for detail.

## 2026-06-22, Library Version 2026.06.222, PR #244

**Codifies the `deep-qa-review` skill (`/full-qa`)** — the AI-failure-pattern half of the trust-recovery escalation tier, and the first codification PR after the trust-recovery suite's sign-off. `deep-qa-review` is a six-subagent forensic QA pass (recent-PR deep review, corpus-wide stale-reference, audit-programme integrity, citation forensic, generated-artefact forensic, discipline-violation forensic) run over a maintainer-named PR window when an AI assistant's discipline failures call for a white-box re-examination beyond the routine sweeps; it pairs with `library-fitness-review` (`/fitness`) to form the suite. The skill bakes in a binding step-0 rule learned from its own first run: verify a full (non-shallow) clone before any git-history-aware audit, because `git log --follow` on a shallow clone mis-attributes last-commit dates and makes gates 31 and 40 emit false positives (iteration 1 caught a 153-document gate-31 false positive this way). Findings route to the backlog top priority tagged `[full-qa]` regardless of severity; the pass terminates on maintainer sign-off, not on an empty finding-set. Shipped with the [`/full-qa` slash command](.claude/commands/full-qa.md) (step-identifier parity 0-6 with the SKILL, enforced by gate 44), the PAIRS-registry extension in [`tools/lint-paired-skill-step-parity.py`](tools/lint-paired-skill-step-parity.py), and the pack-skills enumeration update in [`dev-security/claude-rules/README.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/README.md) (13 to 14 skills). This PR also carries the deferred PR #242 and #243 `/validate-pr` and `/retro` ledger rows per recursion-avoidance. Pack `1.45.2 → 1.46.0`; library `2026.06.221 → 2026.06.222`; README `1.9.92 → 1.9.93`. The ninth governance rule (the `trust-recovery-escalation` rule) and the `/fitness` routing-flag amendment follow in subsequent PRs. See [`.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md`](.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md) for detail.

## 2026-06-22, Library Version 2026.06.217, PR #239

**Closes FR-12 cross-doc follow-up (M, S)** — reconciles [`risk/procedure-risk-register.md`](risk/procedure-risk-register.md) treatment vocabulary with the ERM standard's canonical 6-option set (Avoid / Mitigate / Transfer / Accept / Exploit / Enhance, per the [enterprise risk management standard](risk/standard-enterprise-risk-management.md) §6). The procedure previously listed a different 6-option set (Mitigate / Avoid / Transfer / Accept / Monitor / Further Analysis or Analyze) that conflated workflow states with treatment options. ## 2026-06-22, Library Version 2026.06.216, PR #238

**Closes FR-118 (H, S)** — ERM standard internal §6/§7 treatment-vocab inconsistency resolved in [`risk/standard-enterprise-risk-management.md`](risk/standard-enterprise-risk-management.md) v1.5.1 → 1.6.0. Section 6 (Risk treatment) gains a terminology paragraph distinguishing **Treatment Option** (the risk owner's choice: Avoid / Mitigate / Transfer / Accept / Exploit / Enhance) from **Treatment Status** (workflow state of the option's execution: Pending / In Progress / Complete) and from **Status** (risk-record lifecycle: Open / Closed). Section 7.1 register fields updated: prior single "Status" field with mixed semantics (Open / Mitigated / Accepted / Closed — which conflated treatment outcomes with workflow states) is replaced by three explicit fields: Treatment Option (unchanged from §6's 6 options), new Treatment Status field (Pending / In Progress / Complete), and Status field with cleaned semantics (Open / Closed only, with prose clarifying that Status names risk-record lifecycle and NOT treatment outcome). Closes the structural ambiguity FR-118 surfaced during Pass-2 reshape (where an Avoided risk had no clean Status value other than "Closed"). PR-B in Batch 2 effort-first run. Per-doc `1.5.1 → 1.6.0`. **Closes FR-67 (L, XS)** — adds a new sub-tier **E0: Zero in-house headcount (outsourced contractor)** to the Dimension E (GRC team capacity) ladder in [`docs/template-startup-roadmap.md`](docs/template-startup-roadmap.md). ## 2026-06-22, Library Version 2026.06.211, PR #233

**Closes FR-89 (L, XS) + FR-91 (L, XS)** — security-XS bundle in [`dev-security/standard-api-security.md`](dev-security/standard-api-security.md) (PR-C in Batch 1 effort-first run). JWT algorithm-key-type binding requirement added to the Token validation row of the authentication-controls table (Section 2): validators must verify the JWT `alg` header is consistent with the key type used (RS256 with RSA public key, HS256 with the corresponding shared secret); a single key MUST NOT accept multiple algorithm families. Prevents the RSA-public-key-as-HMAC-secret confusion attack per RFC 8725 (BCP 225, JSON Web Token Best Current Practices). Closes FR-89. Webhook signing row in Section 12 expanded with canonical-string definition (HTTP method + canonical URL path + canonical query string + canonical headers + body hash; both sender and receiver derive the same canonical string) and constant-time comparison requirement (`hmac.compare_digest` or equivalent). Nine sections: (1) joint controller identification (parties, signatories, DPO contacts, EU representatives, lead supervisory authority); (2) joint processing description (purposes, categories, lawful basis, data flows, retention); (3) allocation-of-GDPR-responsibilities table covering every relevant article (6, 9, 10, 13, 14, 15-22, 28, 30, 31, 32, 33, 34, 35, 36, 37-39, 44-49, 26(1) contact point, 26(3) joint-and-several liability) with assignable responsible-party column; (4) operational coordination; (5) liability and indemnification with explicit note that internal indemnity does NOT defeat Article 26(3) joint-and-several liability toward subjects; (6) term and termination; (7) cross-regime alternatives (UK GDPR / LGPD / PIPL / India DPDP / CPPA-PIPEDA / CCPA-CPRA each with notable variations); (8) documentation and audit trail; (9) essence-of-arrangement publication per Article 26(2) naming the 8 elements to publish in each joint controller's privacy notice. Cross-listed in [`privacy/README.md`](privacy/README.md) Active documents (per-doc `1.2.0 → 1.2.1`) and [`governance/register-document-index-and-classification.md`](governance/register-document-index-and-classification.md) (per-doc `1.27.30 → 1.27.31`). ## 2026-06-22, Library Version 2026.06.200, PR #222

**Closes FR-82 (medium, P1.6)**: Clarifies the "AI and Model Data" cryptography row in [`security/policy-encryption-and-key-management.md`](security/policy-encryption-and-key-management.md):56 — the prior text `"AES-256 + key hashing (SHA-512)"` conflated three distinct cryptographic concerns (encryption, integrity, key derivation) under the ambiguous phrase "key hashing". Corrected to: `"AES-256-GCM (AEAD: confidentiality with built-in integrity tag); HKDF-SHA-256 for key derivation from high-entropy material; Argon2id (or scrypt) for password-derived keys. SHA-512 alone is a hash function, not a key-derivation function."` Disambiguates: (a) AES-256-GCM is the AEAD mode pairing confidentiality with built-in integrity (no separate HMAC needed); (b) HKDF-SHA-256 is the standard key-derivation-from-existing-high-entropy-material function per RFC 5869; (c) Argon2id / scrypt are the modern password-based KDFs; (d) explicit note that SHA-512 alone is not a KDF. Per-doc `1.3.1 → 1.3.2`; Date refreshed to 2026-06-22. Also carries the deferred PR #221 /validate-pr history row (0 findings) and /retro register row (no new pattern; Article 36(3) table format flagged as reusable for FR-34 and FR-37 to FR-42). Library `2026.06.199 → 2026.06.200`; README `1.9.70 → 1.9.71`.

## 2026-06-22, Library Version 2026.06.196, PR #218

Corpus prose rename across 73 files: "Chief Privacy Officer" → "Data Protection Officer", with synonym-pattern pre-cleanup collapsing "Chief Privacy Officer / DPO", "Chief Privacy Officer (or Data Protection Officer)", and similar constructs to single canonical form. Approximately 30 `**Owner:**` metadata fields flipped in jurisdiction annexes and a handful of other documents. [`tools/build-portal.py`](tools/build-portal.py) hardcoded string updated; [`docs/portal.md`](docs/portal.md) and [`docs/maturity-scorecard.md`](docs/maturity-scorecard.md) regenerated; [`taxonomy.yml`](taxonomy.yml) regenerated. **PR-2 follows**: adds at-top "Role-name convention" notes in privacy-relevant docs (post-metadata-block placement, pointing to the role authority register for adopter customisation).
